      <p><b>Palestine</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">فلسطين</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Filasṭīn</i>), recognized officially as the <b>State of Palestine</b><sup class="reference" id="ref_naming"><a href="#endnote_naming">[i]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">دولة فلسطين</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Dawlat Filasṭīn</i>) by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and other entities, is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state#De_facto_and_de_jure_states" title="Sovereign state"><i>de jure</i> sovereign state</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> officially governed by the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> and claiming the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a><sup id="cite_ref-only1967_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-only1967-2">[2]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> as the designated capital; in practice, however, only partial administrative control is held over the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_enclaves" title="Palestinian enclaves">167 "islands" in the West Bank</a>, and Gaza is ruled by a rival government (<a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>).<sup class="reference" id="ref_control"><a href="#endnote_control">[iii]</a></sup> The entirety of territory claimed by the State of Palestine has been occupied since 1948, first <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt">by Egypt (Gaza Strip)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian annexation of the West Bank">Jordan (West Bank)</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories" title="Israeli-occupied territories">by Israel</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-Limitations_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Limitations-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Palestine has a population of 5,051,953 as of February 2020, ranked 121st in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, in 1947, the UN adopted a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">Partition Plan</a> for <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a> recommending the creation of independent Arab and Jewish states and an <a href="/wiki/Corpus_separatum_(Jerusalem)" title="Corpus separatum (Jerusalem)">internationalized Jerusalem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181(II)_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181(II)-24">[24]</a></sup> This partition plan was accepted by the Jews but rejected by the Arabs. The day after the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Jewish_state" title="Jewish state">Jewish state</a> in <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">Eretz Israel</a>, to be known as the State of Israel on 14 May 1948,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> neighboring Arab armies <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">invaded</a> the former British mandate and fought the Israeli forces.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Later, the <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">All-Palestine Government</a> was established by the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> on 22 September 1948 to govern the <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Protectorate" title="All-Palestine Protectorate">Egyptian-controlled enclave in Gaza</a>. It was soon recognized by all Arab League members except <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Transjordan</a>. Though jurisdiction of the Government was declared to cover the whole of the former Mandatory Palestine, its effective jurisdiction was limited to the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-gelber177_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gelber177-30">[30]</a></sup> Israel later captured the Gaza Strip and the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai Peninsula</a> from Egypt, the West Bank (including <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a>) from <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a> from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> in June 1967 during the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a>. </p>
      <p>On 15 November 1988 in <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, Chairman of the PLO, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Palestinian Declaration of Independence">proclaimed the establishment of the State of Palestine</a>. A year after the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a> in 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a> was formed to govern (in varying degrees) <a href="/wiki/West_Bank_Areas_in_the_Oslo_II_Accord" title="West Bank Areas in the Oslo II Accord">areas A and B</a> in the West Bank, comprising 165 "islands", and the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>. After Hamas became the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Legislative_Council" title="Palestinian Legislative Council">PNA parliament</a>'s leading party in the most recent elections (2006), a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">conflict</a> broke out between it and the <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> party, leading to Gaza being taken over by Hamas in 2007 (two years after the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza" title="Israeli disengagement from Gaza">Israeli disengagement</a>). </p>
      <p>The State of Palestine has been <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="International recognition of the State of Palestine">recognized by 138 of the 193 UN members</a> and since 2012 has had a status of a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">non-member observer state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charbonneau_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charbonneau-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lederer_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lederer-33">[33]</a></sup> Palestine is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">G77</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a>, and other international bodies. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)#Etymology" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine (region) §&nbsp;Etymology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_name_%22Palestine%22" title="Timeline of the name &quot;Palestine&quot;">Timeline of the name "Palestine"</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Although the concept of the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine region</a> and its geographical extent has varied throughout history, it is now considered to be composed by the modern State of Israel, the West Bank and the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> General use of the term "Palestine" or related terms to the area at the southeast corner of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> beside <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> has <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_name_%22Palestine%22" title="Timeline of the name &quot;Palestine&quot;">historically been taking place</a> since the times of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> being the first historian writing in the 5th century BC in <i><a href="/wiki/Histories_(Herodotus)" title="Histories (Herodotus)">The Histories</a></i> of a "district of Syria, called Palaistine" in which <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> interacted with other maritime peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-Masalha2018_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Masalha2018-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The term "Palestine" (in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>, <i>Palæstina</i>) is thought to have been a term coined by the Ancient Greeks for the area of land occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">Philistines</a>, although there are other explanations.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span></h3> 
      <p>This article uses the terms "Palestine", "State of Palestine", "occupied Palestinian territory" (oPt or OPT) interchangeably depending on context. Specifically, the term "occupied Palestinian territory" refers as a whole to the geographical area of the Palestinian territory occupied by Israel since 1967. In all cases, any references to land or territory refer to land claimed by the State of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="History of the State of Palestine">History of the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Palestine" title="History of Palestine">History of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1947, the UN adopted a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine" title="United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine">partition plan</a> for a two-state solution in the remaining territory of the mandate. The plan was accepted by the Jewish leadership but rejected by the Arab leaders, and Britain refused to implement the plan. On the eve of final British withdrawal, the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Agency_for_Israel" title="Jewish Agency for Israel">Jewish Agency for Israel</a> declared the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="State of Israel">State of Israel</a> according to the proposed UN plan. The <a href="/wiki/Arab_Higher_Committee" title="Arab Higher Committee">Arab Higher Committee</a> did not declare a state of its own and instead, together with <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan" title="Emirate of Transjordan">Transjordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and the other members of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> of the time, commenced military action resulting in the <a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">1948 Arab–Israeli War</a>. During the war, Israel gained additional territories that were designated to be part of the Arab state under the UN plan. Egypt <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by Egypt">occupied</a> the Gaza Strip and Transjordan <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian annexation of the West Bank">occupied and then annexed</a> the West Bank. Egypt initially supported the creation of an <a href="/wiki/All-Palestine_Government" title="All-Palestine Government">All-Palestine Government</a> but disbanded it in 1959. Transjordan never recognized it and instead decided to incorporate the West Bank with its own territory to form <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian annexation of the West Bank">The annexation</a> was ratified in 1950 but was rejected by the international community. The <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> in 1967, when Israel fought against Egypt, Jordan, and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, ended with <a href="/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Israeli occupation of the West Bank">Israel occupying the West Bank</a> and the Gaza Strip, besides other territories.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 1964, when the West Bank was controlled by Jordan, the Palestine Liberation Organization was established there with the goal to confront Israel. The <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Charter" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian National Charter">Palestinian National Charter</a> of the PLO defines the boundaries of Palestine as the whole remaining territory of the mandate, including Israel. Following the Six-Day War, the PLO moved to Jordan, but later relocated to <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> after <a href="/wiki/Black_September_in_Jordan" class="mw-redirect" title="Black September in Jordan">Black September</a> in 1971.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The October <a href="/wiki/1974_Arab_League_summit" title="1974 Arab League summit">1974 Arab League summit</a> designated the PLO as the "sole legitimate representative of the Palestinian people" and reaffirmed "their right to establish an independent state of urgency."<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In November 1974, the PLO was recognized as competent on all matters concerning the question of Palestine by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> granting them <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations#Observers_and_non-members" title="Member states of the United Nations">observer status</a> as a "non-state entity" at the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-GA3237_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA3237-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> After the 1988 Declaration of Independence, the UN General Assembly officially acknowledged the proclamation and decided to use the designation "Palestine" instead of "Palestine Liberation Organization" in the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-GA43177_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA43177-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In spite of this decision, the PLO did not participate at the UN in its capacity of the State of Palestine's government.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1979, through the <a href="/wiki/Camp_David_Accords" title="Camp David Accords">Camp David Accords</a>, Egypt signaled an end to any claim of its own over the Gaza Strip. In July 1988, Jordan <a href="/wiki/Jordan%27s_disengagement_from_the_West_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordan's disengagement from the West Bank">ceded its claims to the West Bank</a>—with the exception of guardianship over <a href="/wiki/Haram_al-Sharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Haram al-Sharif">Haram al-Sharif</a>—to the PLO. In November 1988, the PLO legislature, while in exile, declared the establishment of the "State of Palestine". In the month following, it was quickly recognised by many states, including Egypt and Jordan. In the Palestinian Declaration of Independence, the State of Palestine is described as being established on the "Palestinian territory", without explicitly specifying further. Because of this, some of the countries that recognised the State of Palestine in their statements of recognition refer to the "1967 borders", thus recognizing as its territory only the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">occupied Palestinian territory</a>, and not Israel. The UN membership application submitted by the State of Palestine also specified that it is based on the "1967 borders".<sup id="cite_ref-only1967_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-only1967-2">[2]</a></sup> During the negotiations of the Oslo Accords, the PLO recognised Israel's right to exist, and Israel recognised the PLO as representative of the Palestinian people. Between 1993 and 1998, the PLO made commitments to change the provisions of its Palestinian National Charter that are inconsistent with the aim for a two-state solution and peaceful coexistence with Israel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>After Israel took control of the West Bank from Jordan and Gaza Strip from Egypt, it began to establish <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">Israeli settlements</a> there. These were organised into <a href="/wiki/Judea_and_Samaria_Area" title="Judea and Samaria Area">Judea and Samaria district</a> (West Bank) and <a href="/wiki/Hof_Aza_Regional_Council" title="Hof Aza Regional Council">Hof Aza Regional Council</a> (Gaza Strip) in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_District_(Israel)" title="Southern District (Israel)">Southern District</a>. Administration of the Arab population of these territories was performed by the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Civil_Administration" title="Israeli Civil Administration">Israeli Civil Administration</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Coordinator_of_Government_Activities_in_the_Territories" title="Coordinator of Government Activities in the Territories">Coordinator of Government Activities in the Territories</a> and by local <a href="/wiki/Municipality_(Palestinian_Authority)" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipality (Palestinian Authority)">municipal councils</a> present since before the Israeli takeover. In 1980, Israel decided to freeze elections for these councils and to establish instead Village Leagues, whose officials were under Israeli influence. Later this model became ineffective for both Israel and the Palestinians, and the Village Leagues began to break up, with the last being the Hebron League, dissolved in February 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1993, in the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>, Israel acknowledged the PLO negotiating team as "representing the Palestinian people", in return for the PLO recognizing Israel's right to exist in peace, acceptance of <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council_resolution" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council resolution">UN Security Council resolutions</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 242">242</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_338" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 338">338</a>, and its rejection of "violence and terrorism".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> As a result, in 1994 the PLO established the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a> (PNA or PA) territorial administration, that exercises some governmental functions<sup class="reference" id="ref_control"><a href="#endnote_control">[iii]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Oslo_Accords" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of the Oslo Accords">parts of</a> the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GA52250_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA52250-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007)" title="Battle of Gaza (2007)">takeover</a> of Gaza Strip politically and territorially divided the Palestinians, with <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Abbas</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> left largely ruling the West Bank and recognized internationally as the official <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-alarabiya0701_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alarabiya0701-49">[49]</a></sup> while Hamas secured its <a href="/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Governance of the Gaza Strip">control over the Gaza Strip</a>. In April 2011, the Palestinian parties signed an agreement of <a href="/wiki/Fatah%E2%80%93Hamas_conflict#Reconciliation_attempts" title="Fatah–Hamas conflict">reconciliation</a>, but its implementation had stalled<sup id="cite_ref-alarabiya0701_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alarabiya0701-49">[49]</a></sup> until a <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_government_of_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian government of 2014">unity government</a> was formed on 2 June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Demonstration_against_road_block,_Kafr_Qaddum,_March_2012_3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Demonstration_against_road_block%2C_Kafr_Qaddum%2C_March_2012_3.JPG/220px-Demonstration_against_road_block%2C_Kafr_Qaddum%2C_March_2012_3.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Demonstration_against_road_block%2C_Kafr_Qaddum%2C_March_2012_3.JPG/330px-Demonstration_against_road_block%2C_Kafr_Qaddum%2C_March_2012_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Demonstration_against_road_block%2C_Kafr_Qaddum%2C_March_2012_3.JPG/440px-Demonstration_against_road_block%2C_Kafr_Qaddum%2C_March_2012_3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="3216"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Demonstration_against_road_block,_Kafr_Qaddum,_March_2012_3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Demonstration against road block, <a href="/wiki/Kafr_Qaddum" title="Kafr Qaddum">Kafr Qaddum</a>, March 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As envisioned in the Oslo Accords, Israel allowed the PLO to establish interim administrative institutions in the Palestinian territories, which came in the form of the PNA. It was given civilian control in <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Oslo_Accords" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of the Oslo Accords">Area B</a> and civilian and security control in Area A, and remained without involvement in <a href="/wiki/Area_C_(West_Bank)" title="Area C (West Bank)">Area C</a>. In 2005, following the implementation of Israel's unilateral disengagement plan, the PNA gained full control of the Gaza Strip with the exception of its borders, airspace, and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_waters" title="Territorial waters">territorial waters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="ref_control"><a href="#endnote_control">[iii]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Fatah%E2%80%93Hamas_conflict" title="Fatah–Hamas conflict">inter-Palestinian conflict</a> in 2006, Hamas took over control of the Gaza Strip (it already had majority in the PLC), and Fatah took control of the West Bank. From 2007, the Gaza Strip was <a href="/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Governance of the Gaza Strip">governed by</a> Hamas, and the West Bank by Fatah.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <span class="anchor" id="Politics"></span> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_recognition">International recognition</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="International recognition of the State of Palestine">International recognition of the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The State of Palestine has been <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="International recognition of the State of Palestine">recognized by 138 of the 193 UN members</a> and since 2012 has had a status of a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">non-member observer state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charbonneau_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charbonneau-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lederer_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lederer-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 29 November 2012, in a 138–9 vote (with 41 abstentions and 5 absences),<sup id="cite_ref-GA11317_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA11317-51">[51]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_resolution_67/19" title="United Nations General Assembly resolution 67/19">resolution 67/19</a>, upgrading Palestine from an "observer entity" to a "<a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">non-member observer state</a>" within the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_system" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations system">United Nations system</a>, which was described as recognition of the PLO's sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-Charbonneau_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charbonneau-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lederer_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lederer-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A67L28_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A67L28-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AljazeeraNmChng_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AljazeeraNmChng-54">[54]</a></sup> Palestine's new status is equivalent to that of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hume_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hume-55">[55]</a></sup> The UN has permitted Palestine to title its representative office to the UN as "The Permanent Observer Mission of the State of Palestine to the United Nations",<sup id="cite_ref-un.int_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.int-56">[56]</a></sup> and Palestine has instructed its diplomats to officially represent "The State of Palestine"—no longer the Palestinian National Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-AljazeeraNmChng_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AljazeeraNmChng-54">[54]</a></sup> On 17 December 2012, UN Chief of Protocol Yeocheol Yoon declared that "the designation of 'State of Palestine' shall be used by the Secretariat in all official United Nations documents",<sup id="cite_ref-Gharib_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gharib-57">[57]</a></sup> thus recognising the title 'State of Palestine' as the state's official name for all UN purposes; on 21 December 2012, a UN memorandum discussed appropriate terminology to be used following GA 67/19. It was noted therein that there was no legal impediment to using the designation Palestine to refer to the geographical area of the Palestinian territory. At the same time, it was explained that there was also no bar to the continued use of the term "Occupied Palestinian Territory including East Jerusalem" or such other terminology as might customarily be used by the Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> As of 31 July 2019, 138 (<span data-sort-value="7001715025906735751♠" style="display:none"></span>71.5%) of the 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states">member states</a> of the United Nations have <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="International recognition of the State of Palestine">recognised the State of Palestine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A67L28_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A67L28-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Many of the countries that do not recognise the State of Palestine nevertheless recognise the PLO as the "representative of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian people</a>". The PLO's <a href="/wiki/Executive_Committee_of_the_Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization">Executive Committee</a> is empowered by the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Council" title="Palestinian National Council">Palestinian National Council</a> to perform the functions of government of the State of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-GiE_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiE-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Geography of the State of Palestine">Geography of the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">areas claimed by the State of Palestine</a> lie in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>. The Gaza Strip borders the Mediterranean Sea to the west, Egypt to the south, and Israel to the north and east. The <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> is bordered by Jordan to the east, and Israel to the north, south, and west. Thus, the two enclaves constituting the area claimed by State of Palestine have no geographical border with one another, being separated by Israel. These areas would constitute the world's 163rd largest country by land area.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Palestine has a number of environmental issues; issues facing the Gaza Strip include <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>; <a href="/wiki/Biosalinity" title="Biosalinity">salination</a> of fresh water; <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">sewage treatment</a>; <a href="/wiki/Water-borne_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Water-borne disease">water-borne diseases</a>; <a href="/wiki/Soil_degradation" class="mw-redirect" title="Soil degradation">soil degradation</a>; and depletion and contamination of underground water resources. In the West Bank, many of the same issues apply; although fresh water is much more plentiful, access is restricted by the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories#Political_status_and_sovereignty" title="Palestinian territories">dispute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-al_Haq_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-al_Haq-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three terrestrial ecoregions are found in the area: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_conifer-sclerophyllous-broadleaf_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Mediterranean conifer-sclerophyllous-broadleaf forests">Eastern Mediterranean conifer-sclerophyllous-broadleaf forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamian_shrub_desert" title="Mesopotamian shrub desert">Mesopotamian shrub desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <p>Temperatures in Palestine vary widely. The climate in the West Bank is mostly <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a>, slightly cooler at elevated areas compared with the shoreline, west to the area. In the east, the West Bank includes much of the Judean Desert including the western shoreline of the Dead Sea, characterised by dry and hot climate. Gaza has a <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">hot semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: BSh) with mild winters and dry hot summers.<sup id="cite_ref-GS_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GS-65">[65]</a></sup> Spring arrives around March–April and the hottest months are July and August, with the average high being 33&nbsp;°C (91&nbsp;°F). The coldest month is January with temperatures usually at 7&nbsp;°C (45&nbsp;°F). Rain is scarce and generally falls between November and March, with annual precipitation rates approximately at 4.57 inches (116&nbsp;mm).<sup id="cite_ref-MSN_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSN-66">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_government" title="Palestinian government">Palestinian government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Palestine" title="Elections in Palestine">Elections in Palestine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Next_Palestinian_general_election" class="mw-redirect" title="Next Palestinian general election">Next Palestinian general election</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Politics of the Palestinian National Authority">Politics of the Palestinian National Authority</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Palestine_Liberation_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Politics of the Palestine Liberation Organization">Politics of the Palestine Liberation Organization</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg/220px-PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg/330px-PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg/440px-PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="378"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:PalestinianLegislativeCouncilGazaCity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The destroyed <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Legislative_Council" title="Palestinian Legislative Council">Palestinian Legislative Council</a> building in Gaza City, <a href="/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Israel_conflict" title="Gaza–Israel conflict">Gaza–Israel conflict</a>, September 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The State of Palestine consists of the following institutions that are associated with the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> (PLO): </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="President of the State of Palestine">President of the State of Palestine</a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_PLOChair"><a href="#endnote_PLOChair">[iv]</a></sup>&nbsp;– appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Central_Council" title="Palestinian Central Council">Palestinian Central Council</a><sup id="cite_ref-p2008_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2008-68">[68]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Council" title="Palestinian National Council">Palestinian National Council</a>&nbsp;– the legislature that established the State of Palestine<sup id="cite_ref-declaration1988_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-declaration1988-5">[5]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Executive_Committee_of_the_Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization">Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization</a>&nbsp;– performs the functions of a government in exile,<sup id="cite_ref-A67L28_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A67L28-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GiE_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiE-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unescogie_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescogie-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> maintaining an extensive foreign-relations network</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>These should be distinguished from the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="President of the Palestinian National Authority">President of the Palestinian National Authority</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Legislative_Council" title="Palestinian Legislative Council">Palestinian Legislative Council</a> (PLC) and <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_government_of_June_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian government of June 2007">PNA Cabinet</a>, all of which are instead associated with the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a>. </p>
      <p>The State of Palestine's founding document is the Palestinian Declaration of Independence,<sup id="cite_ref-declaration1988_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-declaration1988-5">[5]</a></sup> and it should be distinguished from the unrelated PLO <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Covenant" title="Palestinian National Covenant">Palestinian National Covenant</a> and PNA <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Basic_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestine Basic Law">Palestine Basic Law</a>. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">

      <p>a. Data from Jerusalem includes occupied <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a> with its Israeli population </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png/170px-Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png/255px-Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png/340px-Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png 2x" data-file-width="3130" data-file-height="5106"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Westbank_Control_%26_Access_Restrictions_Dec_2012.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">Israeli settlements</a> in the West Bank
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The governorates in the West Bank are grouped into <a href="/wiki/West_Bank_Areas_in_the_Oslo_II_Accord" title="West Bank Areas in the Oslo II Accord">three areas per the Oslo II Accord</a>. Area A forms 18% of the West Bank by area, and is administered by the Palestinian government.<sup id="cite_ref-Zahriyeh2014_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahriyeh2014-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gvirtzman_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gvirtzman-73">[73]</a></sup> Area B forms 22% of the West Bank, and is under Palestinian civil control, and joint Israeli-Palestinian security control.<sup id="cite_ref-Zahriyeh2014_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahriyeh2014-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gvirtzman_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gvirtzman-73">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Area_C_(West_Bank)" title="Area C (West Bank)">Area C</a>, except <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a>, forms 60% of the West Bank, and is administered by the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Civil_Administration" title="Israeli Civil Administration">Israeli Civil Administration</a>, except that the Palestinian government provides the education and medical services to the 150,000 Palestinians in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Zahriyeh2014_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahriyeh2014-72">[72]</a></sup> More than 99% of Area C is off limits to Palestinians.<sup id="cite_ref-WBAUS2922_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WBAUS2922-74">[74]</a></sup> There are about 330,000 Israelis living in <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">settlements</a> in Area C,<sup id="cite_ref-CBS2010_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS2010-75">[75]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Judea_and_Samaria_Area" title="Judea and Samaria Area">Judea and Samaria Area</a>. Although Area C is under <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">martial law</a>, Israelis living there are judged in Israeli civil courts.<sup id="cite_ref-CERD1416_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CERD1416-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>East Jerusalem (comprising the small pre-1967 Jordanian eastern-sector Jerusalem municipality together with a significant area of the pre-1967 West Bank demarcated by Israel in 1967) is administered as part of the <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_District" title="Jerusalem District">Jerusalem District</a> of Israel but is claimed by Palestine as part of the <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerusalem Governorate">Jerusalem Governorate</a>. It was effectively annexed by Israel in 1967, by application of Israeli law, jurisdiction and administration under a 1948 law amended for the purpose, this purported annexation being constitutionally reaffirmed (by implication) in Basic Law: Jerusalem 1980,<sup id="cite_ref-Zahriyeh2014_72-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahriyeh2014-72">[72]</a></sup> but this annexation is not recognised by any other country.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In 2010 of the 456,000 people in East Jerusalem, roughly 60% were Palestinians and 40% were Israelis.<sup id="cite_ref-Zahriyeh2014_72-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zahriyeh2014-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChoshenEtKorach2010_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChoshenEtKorach2010-78">[78]</a></sup> However, since the late 2000s, Israel's <a href="/wiki/West_Bank_Security_Barrier" class="mw-redirect" title="West Bank Security Barrier">West Bank Security Barrier</a> has effectively re-annexed tens of thousands of Palestinians bearing Israeli ID cards to the West Bank, leaving East Jerusalem within the barrier with a small Israeli majority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Palestine" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign relations of Palestine">Foreign relations of Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Palestine" class="mw-redirect" title="List of diplomatic missions of Palestine">List of diplomatic missions of Palestine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_to_Palestine" class="mw-redirect" title="List of diplomatic missions to Palestine">List of diplomatic missions to Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Representation of the State of Palestine is performed by the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> (PLO). In states that recognise the State of Palestine it maintains <a href="/wiki/Embassy" class="mw-redirect" title="Embassy">embassies</a>. The Palestine Liberation Organization is represented in various international organizations as member, associate or observer. Because of inconclusiveness in sources in some cases it is impossible to distinguish whether the participation is executed by the PLO as representative of the State of Palestine, by the PLO as a non-state entity or by the PNA.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_recognition_2">International recognition</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palestine_recognition_only.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Palestine_recognition_only.svg/350px-Palestine_recognition_only.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Palestine_recognition_only.svg/525px-Palestine_recognition_only.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Palestine_recognition_only.svg/700px-Palestine_recognition_only.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1314"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Palestine_recognition_only.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>International recognition of the State of Palestine
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="International recognition of the State of Palestine">International recognition of the State of Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestine_194" title="Palestine 194">Palestine 194</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 15 December 1988, the State of Palestine's <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Palestinian Declaration of Independence">declaration of independence</a> of November 1988 was acknowledged in the General Assembly with <a href="/wiki/Resolution_43/177" class="mw-redirect" title="Resolution 43/177">Resolution 43/177</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 31 July 2019, 138 (<span data-sort-value="7001715025906735751♠" style="display:none"></span>71.5%) of the 193 member states of the United Nations have recognised the State of Palestine. Many of the countries that do not recognise the State of Palestine nevertheless recognise the PLO as the "representative of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian people</a>". The PLO's <a href="/wiki/Executive_Committee_of_the_Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization">executive committee</a> is empowered by the PNC to perform the functions of government of the State of Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-GiE_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiE-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 29 November 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-GA11317_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA11317-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly_resolution_67/19" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly resolution 67/19">UN General Assembly resolution 67/19</a> passed, upgrading Palestine to "<a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">non-member observer state</a>" status in the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-A67L28_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A67L28-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AljazeeraNmChng_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AljazeeraNmChng-54">[54]</a></sup> The change in status was described as "<i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> recognition of the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Palestine".<sup id="cite_ref-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 3 October 2014, new <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swedish</a> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Stefan_L%C3%B6fven" title="Stefan Löfven">Stefan Löfven</a> used his inaugural address in parliament to announce that Sweden would recognise the state of Palestine. The official decision to do so was made on 30 October, making Sweden the first EU member state outside of the former communist bloc to recognise the state of Palestine. Most of the EU's 27 member states have refrained from recognising Palestinian statehood and those that do—such as Hungary, Poland, and Slovakia—did so before accession.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 October 2014, the UK House of Commons voted by 274 to 12 in favour of recognising Palestine as a state.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The House of Commons backed the move "as a contribution to securing a negotiated two-state solution"—although less than half of MPs took part in the vote. However, the UK government is not bound to do anything as a result of the vote: its current policy is that it "reserves the right to recognise a Palestinian state bilaterally at the moment of our choosing and when it can best help bring about peace".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 2 December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(France)" title="National Assembly (France)">French parliament</a> voted by 331 to 151 in favour of urging their government to recognise Palestine as a state. The text, proposed by the ruling Socialists and backed by left-wing parties and some conservatives, asked the government to "use the recognition of a Palestinian state with the aim of resolving the conflict definitively".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 December 2014, the United Nations Security Council voted down a resolution demanding the end of Israeli occupation and statehood by 2017. Eight members voted for the Resolution (Russia, China, France, Argentina, Chad, Chile, Jordan, Luxembourg), however following strenuous US and Israeli efforts to defeat the resolution,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> it did not get the minimum of nine votes needed to pass the resolution. Australia and the United States voted against the resolution, with five other nations abstaining.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Al-Khader.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Al-Khader.jpg/220px-Al-Khader.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Al-Khader.jpg/330px-Al-Khader.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Al-Khader.jpg/440px-Al-Khader.jpg 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Al-Khader.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Children waving a Palestinian flag, West Bank
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 10 January 2015, the first Palestinian embassy in a western European country is opened in Stockholm, Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 16 January 2015, the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> announced that, since Palestine was granted observer State status in the UN by the UNGA, it must be considered a "State" for the purposes of accession to the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 13 May 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> announced it was shifting recognition from the PLO to the State of Palestine, confirming recognition of Palestine as a state after the UN vote of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Monsignor Antoine Camilleri, Vatican foreign minister, said the change was in line with the evolving position of the Holy See, which has referred unofficially to the State of Palestine since <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a>'s visit to the Holy Land in May 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 23 December 2015, the UN General Assembly adopted a resolution demanding Palestinian sovereignty over the natural resources in the Palestinian territories under Israeli occupation. It called on Israel to desist from the exploitation, damage, cause of loss or depletion and endangerment of Palestinian natural resources, the right of Palestinians to seek restitution for extensive destruction. The motion was passed by 164 votes to 5, with Canada, <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>, Israel, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, and the United States opposing.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Raising_the_flag_at_the_UN">Raising the flag at the UN</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Palestine_and_the_United_Nations" title="Palestine and the United Nations">Palestine and the United Nations</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In August 2015, Palestine's representatives at the UN presented a draft resolution that would allow the non-member observer states Palestine and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> to raise their flags at the United Nations headquarters. Initially, the Palestinians presented their initiative as a joint effort with the Holy See, which the Holy See denied.<sup id="cite_ref-i24_un_flag_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i24_un_flag-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In a letter to the Secretary General and the President of the General Assembly, Israel's Ambassador at the UN <a href="/wiki/Ron_Prosor" title="Ron Prosor">Ron Prosor</a> called the step "another cynical misuse of the UN ... in order to score political points".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the vote, which was passed by 119 votes to 8 with 45 countries abstaining,<sup id="cite_ref-cnnUN_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnUN-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> the US Ambassador Samantha Power said that "raising the Palestinian flag will not bring Israelis and Palestinians any closer together".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> US Department of State spokesman Mark Toner called it a "counterproductive" attempt to pursue statehood claims outside of a negotiated settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-aj_un_flag_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aj_un_flag-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the ceremony itself, U.N. Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> said the occasion was a "day of pride for the Palestinian people around the world, a day of hope",<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and declared "Now is the time to restore confidence by both Israelis and Palestinians for a peaceful settlement and, at last, the realization of two states for two peoples."<sup id="cite_ref-cnnUN_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnUN-97">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status">Legal status</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Legal_status_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Legal status of the State of Palestine">Legal status of the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are a wide variety of views regarding the status of the State of Palestine, both among the states of the international community and among legal scholars. The existence of a state of Palestine, although controversial, is a reality in the opinions of the states that have established bilateral diplomatic relations.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boyle_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyle-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DugardOpEd_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DugardOpEd-106">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_security">Law and security</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Security_Services" title="Palestinian Security Services">Palestinian Security Services</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Crime in the State of Palestine">Crime in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The State of Palestine has a number of security forces, including a <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Civil_Police_Force" title="Palestinian Civil Police Force">Civil Police Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Security_Forces" title="Palestinian National Security Forces">National Security Forces</a> and Intelligence Services, with the function of maintaining security and protecting Palestinian citizens and the Palestinian State. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Demographics of the State of Palestine">Demographics of the State of Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Palestine_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of regions of Palestine by Human Development Index">List of regions of Palestine by Human Development Index</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-108">[108]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.9 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">3.2 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">4.9 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>According to the Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics, the State of Palestine had <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> of 4,420,549 people in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-census_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-109">[109]</a></sup> Within an area of 6,020 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (2,320&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">sq&nbsp;mi</a>), there is a <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of about 827 people per square kilometre.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-62">[62]</a></sup> To put this in a wider context, the average population density of the world was 25 people per square kilometre as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Healthcare in the State of Palestine">Healthcare in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the Palestinian Ministry of Health (MOH), as of 2017, there were 743 primary health care centers in Palestine (583 in the West Bank and 160 in Gaza), and 81 hospitals (51 in the West Bank, including East Jerusalem, and 30 in Gaza).<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Operating under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO),<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> the Health Cluster for the occupied Palestinian territory (oPt) was established in 2009 and represents a partnership of over 70 local and international nongovernmental organisations and UN agencies providing a framework for health actors involved in the humanitarian response for the oPt. The Cluster is co-chaired by the MOH to ensure alignment with national policies and plans.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The report of WHO Director-General of 1 May 2019 describes health sector conditions in the oPt identifying strategic priorities and current obstacles to their achievement<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> pursuant to the country cooperation strategy for WHO and the Occupied Palestinian Territory 2017–2020.<sup id="cite_ref-CCS2020_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCS2020-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Education in the State of Palestine">Education in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The literacy rate of Palestine was 96.3% according to a 2014 report by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>, which is high by international standards. There is a gender difference in the population aged above 15 with 5.9% of women considered illiterate compared to 1.6% of men.<sup id="cite_ref-undp_palestine_education_2014_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp_palestine_education_2014-116">[116]</a></sup> Illiteracy among women has fallen from 20.3% in 1997 to less than 6% in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-undp_palestine_education_2014_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp_palestine_education_2014-116">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Freedom of religion in the State of Palestine">Freedom of religion in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
