      <p>93% of Palestinians are Muslim,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> the vast majority of whom are followers of the <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> with a small minority of <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and 15% being <a href="/wiki/Nondenominational_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Nondenominational Muslims">nondenominational Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Christian">Palestinian Christians</a> represent a significant minority of 6%, followed by much smaller <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious</a> communities, including <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Samaritans" title="Samaritans">Samaritans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Salome2010_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salome2010-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Economy of the State of Palestine">Economy of the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Tourism in the State of Palestine">Tourism in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism in the territory claimed by the State of Palestine refers to <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Jerusalem" title="East Jerusalem">East Jerusalem</a>, the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>. In 2010, 4.6 million people visited the Palestinian territories, compared to 2.6 million in 2009. Of that number, 2.2 million were foreign tourists while 2.7 million were domestic.<sup id="cite_ref-PCBS_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCBS-122">[122]</a></sup> Most tourists come for only a few hours or as part of a day trip itinerary. In the last quarter of 2012 over 150,000 guests stayed in West Bank hotels; 40% were European and 9% were from the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Lonely Planet travel guide writes that "the West Bank is not the easiest place in which to travel but the effort is richly rewarded."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-124">[124]</a></sup> In 2013 Palestinian Authority Tourism minister <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rula_Ma%27ay%27a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rula Ma'ay'a (page does not exist)">Rula Ma'ay'a</a> stated that her government aims to encourage international visits to Palestine, but the occupation is the main factor preventing the tourism sector from becoming a major income source to Palestinians.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> There are no visa conditions imposed on foreign nationals other than those imposed by&nbsp;the visa policy of Israel. Access to&nbsp;Jerusalem, the&nbsp;West Bank, and Gaza&nbsp;is completely controlled by the Government of Israel. Entry to the occupied Palestinian territories requires only a valid international passport.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Communications in the State of Palestine">Communications in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Central_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics">Palestinian Central Bureau of Statistics</a> (PCBS) and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Telecom_and_Information_Technology_of_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Ministry of Telecom and Information Technology of the State of Palestine">Ministry of Telecom and Information Technology</a> said there were 4.2 million cellular mobile subscribers in Palestine compared to 2.6 million at the end of 2010 while the number of ADSL subscribers in Palestine increased to about 363 thousand by the end of 2019 from 119 thousand over the same period. 97% of Palestinian households have at least one cellular mobile line while at least one smartphone is owned by 86% of households (91% in the West Bank and 78% in Gaza Strip). About 80% of the Palestinian households have access to the internet in their homes and about a third have a computer.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> On 12 June 2020, the World Bank approved a US$15 million grant for the Technology for Youth and Jobs (TechStart) Project aiming to help the Palestinian IT sector upgrade the capabilities of firms and create more high-quality jobs. Kanthan Shankar, World Bank Country Director for West Bank and Gaza said "The IT sector has the potential to make a strong contribution to economic growth. It can offer opportunities to Palestinian youth, who constitute 30% of the population and suffer from acute unemployment."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Monetary_Authority" title="Palestine Monetary Authority">Palestine Monetary Authority</a> has issued guidelines for the operation and provision of electronic payment services including e-wallet and prepaid cards.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Transport in the State of Palestine">Transport in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="Water supply and sanitation in the State of Palestine">Water supply and sanitation in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Water,_Sanitation_and_Hygiene_Monitoring_Program" title="Water, Sanitation and Hygiene Monitoring Program">Water, Sanitation and Hygiene Monitoring Program</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Water supply and sanitation in the Palestinian territories are characterized by severe water shortage and are highly influenced by the Israeli occupation. The water resources of Palestine are fully controlled by Israel and the division of groundwater is subject to provisions in the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_II_Accord" title="Oslo II Accord">Oslo II Accord</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Generally, the water quality is considerably worse in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_strip" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaza strip">Gaza strip</a> when compared to the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>. About a third to half of the delivered water in the Palestinian territories is <a href="/wiki/Non-revenue_water" title="Non-revenue water">lost in the distribution network</a>. The lasting blockade of the Gaza Strip and the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaza War (2008–09)">Gaza War</a> have caused severe damage to the infrastructure in the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Gaza_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Gaza-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Concerning wastewater, the existing treatment plants do not have the capacity to treat all of the produced wastewater, causing severe water pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The development of the sector highly depends on external financing.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Palestine" title="Culture of Palestine">Culture of Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="List of World Heritage Sites in the State of Palestine">List of World Heritage Sites in the State of Palestine</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <p>There are a number of newspapers, news agencies, and satellite television stations in the State of Palestine. News agencies include <a href="/wiki/Ma%27an_News_Agency" title="Ma'an News Agency">Ma'an News Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wafa" title="Wafa">Wafa</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palestine_News_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palestine News Network (page does not exist)">Palestine News Network</a> and the satellite television includes <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_TV" title="Al-Aqsa TV">Al-Aqsa TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Quds_TV" title="Al-Quds TV">Al-Quds TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanabel_TV" title="Sanabel TV">Sanabel TV</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <p>Football (Soccer in the United States) is the most popular sport among the Palestinian people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Rugby is also a popular sport.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Palestine_national_football_team" title="Palestine national football team">Palestine national football team</a> represents the country in international football. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <table style="margin-left:13px; line-height:150%;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:top;">i.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_naming"><b><a href="#ref_naming">^</a></b></span> Note that the name <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a> can commonly be interpreted as the entire territory of the former <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">British Mandate</a>, which today also incorporates Israel. The history was expressed by Mahmoud Abbas in his September 2011 speech to the United Nations: "... we agreed to establish the State of Palestine on only 22% of the territory of historical Palestine—on all the Palestinian Territory occupied by Israel in 1967."<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The name is also officially used as the short-form reference to the State of Palestine<sup id="cite_ref-Bissiop433_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bissiop433-3">[3]</a></sup> and this should be distinguished from other homonymous uses for the term including the Palestinian Authority,<sup id="cite_ref-Pagep161_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pagep161-135">[135]</a></sup> the Palestine Liberation Organization,<sup id="cite_ref-GA43177_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA43177-42">[42]</a></sup> and the subject of other <a href="/wiki/Proposals_for_a_Palestinian_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposals for a Palestinian state">proposals for the establishment of a Palestinian state</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:top;">ii.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_capital"><b><a href="#ref_capital">^</a></b></span> The <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Palestinian Declaration of Independence">Palestinian Declaration of Independence</a> proclaims the "establishment of the State of Palestine on our Palestinian territory with its capital Jerusalem (Al-Quds Ash-Sharif)."<sup id="cite_ref-declaration1988_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-declaration1988-5">[5]</a></sup> The same decision was taken also by the PLC in May 2002 when it approved the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_Law#Basic_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian Law">PNA Basic Law</a>, which states unambiguously "Jerusalem is the Capital of Palestine".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative capital where government institutions and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_to_Palestine" class="mw-redirect" title="List of diplomatic missions to Palestine">foreign representative offices</a> are located. Jerusalem's final status awaits future negotiations between Israel and the Palestinian Authority (see <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r999302996">.mw-parser-output cite.citation{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .citation q{quotes:"\"""\"""'""'"}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-free a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-free a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Lock-green.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .id-lock-registration a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-limited a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-registration a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Lock-gray-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .id-lock-subscription a,.mw-parser-output .citation .cs1-lock-subscription a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Lock-red-alt-2.svg")right 0.1em center/9px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration{color:#555}.mw-parser-output .cs1-subscription span,.mw-parser-output .cs1-registration span{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}.mw-parser-output .cs1-ws-icon a{background:linear-gradient(transparent,transparent),url("//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg")right 0.1em center/12px no-repeat}.mw-parser-output code.cs1-code{color:inherit;background:inherit;border:none;padding:inherit}.mw-parser-output .cs1-hidden-error{display:none;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-visible-error{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{display:none;color:#33aa33;margin-left:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-format{font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}</style><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060514191731/http://www.publicpolicy.umd.edu/IPPP/Fall97Report/negotiating_jerusalem.htm">"Negotiating Jerusalem"</a>. University of Maryland. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.publicpolicy.umd.edu/IPPP/Fall97Report/negotiating_jerusalem.htm">the original</a> on 14 May 2006<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">5 August</span> 2009</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Negotiating+Jerusalem&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Maryland&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.publicpolicy.umd.edu%2FIPPP%2FFall97Report%2Fnegotiating_jerusalem.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AState+of+Palestine" class="Z3988"></span>). The United Nations and most countries do not accept Israel's annexation of East Jerusalem through the <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Law" title="Jerusalem Law">Jerusalem Law</a> of 1980 (see <a href="#CITEREFKellerman1993">Kellerman 1993</a>, p.&nbsp;140) and maintain their <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Israel" title="List of diplomatic missions in Israel">embassies to Israel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> (see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/the-world-factbook/countries/israel/"><i>The World Factbook</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a>). The international community also does not recognize either Israeli or Palestinian sovereignty over Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:top;">iii.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_control"><b><a href="#ref_control">^</a></b></span> Israel allows the PNA to execute some functions in the Palestinian territories, depending on the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Oslo_Accords" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of the Oslo Accords">area classification</a>. It maintains minimal interference (retaining control of borders: <a href="/wiki/National_airspace" class="mw-redirect" title="National airspace">air</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GazaSeaAir_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazaSeaAir-138">[138]</a></sup> sea beyond <a href="/wiki/Internal_waters" title="Internal waters">internal waters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-GazaSeaAir_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazaSeaAir-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Border_Assistance_Mission_Rafah" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union Border Assistance Mission Rafah">land</a><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>) in the Gaza Strip (its interior and Egypt portion of the land border are under <a href="/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Governance of the Gaza Strip">Hamas control</a>), and varying degrees of interference elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-HumanRightsWatch_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HumanRightsWatch-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> See also <a href="/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories" title="Israeli-occupied territories">Israeli-occupied territories</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:top;">iv.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_PLOChair"><b><a href="#ref_PLOChair">^</a></b></span> So far both presidents of the State of Palestine, <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> and his successor <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, were appointed beforehand as <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Executive_Committee_of_the_Palestine_Liberation_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman of the Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization">Chairman of the Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Committee_of_the_Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Executive Committee of the Palestine Liberation Organization">committee</a> performing the functions of State of Palestine government.<sup id="cite_ref-A67L28_53-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A67L28-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GiE_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GiE-60">[60]</a></sup> See also <a href="/wiki/Leaders_of_Palestinian_institutions" title="Leaders of Palestinian institutions">Leaders of Palestinian institutions</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:top;">v.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_NewTestament"><b><a href="#ref_NewTestament">^</a></b></span> The <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a>, taking up a term used once in the <a href="/wiki/Tanakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanakh">Tanakh</a> (1 Samuel 13:19),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhitelam199640–42_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhitelam199640–42-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasalha200732_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasalha200732-147">[147]</a></sup> speaks of a larger theologically-defined area, of which Palestine is a part, as the "land of Israel"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESaldarini199428–29_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESaldarini199428–29-148">[148]</a></sup> (γῆ Ἰσραήλ) (<a href="/wiki/Matthew_2:20%E2%80%9321" title="Matthew 2:20–21">Matthew 2:20–21</a>), in a narrative paralleling that of the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Exodus" title="Book of Exodus">Book of Exodus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg2001147_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg2001147-149">[149]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:top;">vi.&nbsp;&nbsp; </td> 
         <td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Strabo"><b><a href="#ref_Strabo">^</a></b></span> Other writers, such as <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>, referred to the region as <i><a href="/wiki/Coele-Syria" title="Coele-Syria">Coele-Syria</a></i> ("all Syria") around 10–20 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldman1996557–58_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldman1996557–58-150">[150]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>

        <li id="cite_note-Lapidoth-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Lapidoth_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFLapidoth2011" class="citation web cs1"><a href="/wiki/Ruth_Lapidoth" title="Ruth Lapidoth">Lapidoth, Ruth</a> (2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140605013337/http://www.jiis.org/.upload/lapidoth-jerusalem.pdf">"Jerusalem: Some Legal Issues"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>The Jerusalem Institute for Israel Studies</i>. p.&nbsp;26. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jiis.org/.upload/lapidoth-jerusalem.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 5 June 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">5 June</span> 2014</span>. <q>The attitude of the Palestinians was expressed inter alia in 1988 and 2002. When the Palestine National Council proclaimed in November 1988 the establishment of a Palestinian State, it asserted that Jerusalem was its capital. In October 2002, the Palestinian Legislative Council adopted the Law on the Capital, which stipulates that Jerusalem is the capital of the Palestinian State, the main seat of its three branches of government. The State of Palestine is the sovereign of Jerusalem and of its holy places. Any statute or agreement that diminishes the rights of the Palestinian State in Jerusalem is invalid. This statute can be amended only with the consent of two-thirds of the members of the Legislative Council. The 2003 Basic Law also asserts that Jerusalem is the capital of the State of Palestine.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Jerusalem+Institute+for+Israel+Studies&amp;rft.atitle=Jerusalem%3A+Some+Legal+Issues&amp;rft.pages=26&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.aulast=Lapidoth&amp;rft.aufirst=Ruth&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.jiis.org%2F.upload%2Flapidoth-jerusalem.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AState+of+Palestine" class="Z3988"></span> Reprinted from: <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCdiger_Wolfrum" title="Rüdiger Wolfrum">Wolfrum, Rüdiger</a> (ed.) (online 2008, print 2011). <i><a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Encyclopedia_of_Public_International_Law" title="Max Planck Encyclopedia of Public International Law">The Max Planck Encyclopedia of Public International Law</a></i>. Oxford University Press.</span> </li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">16 December</span> 2020</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Human+Development+Report+2020+The+Next+Frontier%3A+Human+Development+and+the+Anthropocene&amp;rft.pages=343-346&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations+Development+Programme&amp;rft.date=2020-12-15&amp;rft.isbn=978-92-1-126442-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fhdr.undp.org%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Fhdr2020.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AState+of+Palestine" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mfa.gov.il/MFA/Peace+Process/Guide+to+the+Peace+Process/Gaza-Jericho+Agreement+Annex+IV+-+Economic+Protoco.htm">Article 4 of the 1994 Paris Protocol</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20161001065601/http://www.mfa.gov.il/MFA/Peace%2BProcess/Guide%2Bto%2Bthe%2BPeace%2BProcess/Gaza-Jericho%2BAgreement%2BAnnex%2BIV%2B-%2BEconomic%2BProtoco.htm">Archived</a> 1 October 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. The Protocol allows the Palestinian Authority to adopt multiple currencies. In the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>, the Israeli new sheqel and Jordanian dinar are widely accepted; while in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, the Israeli new sheqel and Egyptian pound are widely accepted.</span> </li>

        <li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldberg2001147-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldberg2001147_149-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGoldberg2001">Goldberg 2001</a>, p.&nbsp;147: "The parallels between this narrative and that of Exodus continue to be drawn. Like Pharaoh before him, Herod, having been frustrated in his original efforts, now seeks to achieve his objectives by implementing a program of infanticide. As a result, here—as in Exodus—rescuing the hero's life from the clutches of the evil king necessitates a sudden flight to another country. And finally, in perhaps the most vivid parallel of all, the present narrative uses virtually the same words of the earlier one to provide the information that the coast is clear for the herds safe return: here, in Matthew 2:20, "go [back]… for those who sought the Childs life are dead; there, in Exodus 4:19, go back… for all the men who sought your life are dead."<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> sfn error: no target: CITEREFGoldberg2001 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span></span> </li>

         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFPeters1992" class="citation book cs1">Peters, Joel (1992). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/israelafricap00pete"><i>Israel and Africa: The Problematic Friendship</i></a> (illustrated&nbsp;ed.). <a href="/wiki/I.B.Tauris" class="mw-redirect" title="I.B.Tauris">I.B.Tauris</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-870915-10-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-870915-10-6"><bdi>978-1-870915-10-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Israel+and+Africa%3A+The+Problematic+Friendship&amp;rft.edition=illustrated&amp;rft.pub=I.B.Tauris&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-870915-10-6&amp;rft.aulast=Peters&amp;rft.aufirst=Joel&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Fisraelafricap00pete&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AState+of+Palestine" class="Z3988"></span></li> 
        <li>Shatz, Adam, "We Are Conquerors" (review of <a href="/wiki/Tom_Segev" title="Tom Segev">Tom Segev</a>, <i>A State at Any Cost: The Life of David Ben-Gurion</i>, Head of Zeus, 2019, 804 pp., 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-78954-462-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-78954-462-6">978-1-78954-462-6</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/London_Review_of_Books" title="London Review of Books">London Review of Books</a></i>, vol. 41, no. 20 (24 October 2019), pp. 37–38, 40–42. "Segev's biography... shows how central exclusionary <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> were to <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">Ben-Gurion</a>'s vision of the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_homeland" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish homeland">Jewish homeland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>, and how contemptuous he was not only of the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> but of Jewish life outside <a href="/wiki/Zion" title="Zion">Zion</a>. [Liberal Jews] may look at the state that Ben-Gurion built, and ask if the cost has been worth it." (p. 42 of Shatz's review.)</li> 
        <li>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFTaylor_&amp;_Francis_GroupDean2003" class="citation book cs1">Taylor &amp; Francis Group; Dean, Lucy (2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pP315Mw3S9EC&amp;pg=PA1328"><i>The Middle East and North Africa 2004: 2004</i></a> (illustrated&nbsp;ed.). <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-85743-184-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-85743-184-1"><bdi>978-1-85743-184-1</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Middle+East+and+North+Africa+2004%3A+2004&amp;rft.edition=illustrated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-85743-184-1&amp;rft.au=Taylor+%26+Francis+Group&amp;rft.au=Dean%2C+Lucy&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DpP315Mw3S9EC%26pg%3DPA1328&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AState+of+Palestine" class="Z3988"></span></li>
